  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a78090f2-e1af-4f4a-a808-37a278eb7108'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText16487845611599463935" style="display:none">At fourteen, Nick Gautier thinks he knows everything about the world around him. Streetwise, tough and savvy, his quick sarcasm is the stuff of legends. . .until the night when his best friends try to kill him. Saved by a mysterious warrior who has more fighting skills than Chuck Norris, Nick is sucked into the realm of the Dark-Hunters: immortal vampire slayers who risk everything to save humanity. <br /><br />Nick quickly learns that the human world is only a veil for a much larger and more dangerous one: a world where the captain of the football team is a werewolf and the girl he has a crush on goes out at night to stake the undead. But before he can even learn the rules of this new world, his fellow students are turning into flesh eating zombies. And he's next on the menu. <br /><br />As if starting high school isn't hard enough. . .now Nick has to hide his new friends from his mom, his chainsaw from the principal, and keep the zombies and the demon Simi from eating his brains, all without getting grounded or suspended. How in the world is he supposed to do that?</span>

<div id="review_139398788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139398788" />
    <a title="Georgia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4380124-georgia"><img alt="Georgia" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139398788?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Georgia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Georgia" href="/user/show/4380124-georgia">Georgia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4380124-georgia?shelf=didn-t-finish">didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139398788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2024584752295162237">THE WORST BOOK I HAVE EVER READ.<br/>The writing is stilted, the story is dull, it doesn't make sense. The main character is a complete waste of space - I didn't like him at all, and was glad when bad things happened to him. There is no explanation for anything, and things happen for no reason at all; nothing is ever explained, or acknowledged. Things just happen, and are put across in this terrible attempt-funny style of writing that's just disjointed and lazy. Not to mention that the protag's condi</span>
  <span id="freeText2024584752295162237" style="display:none">THE WORST BOOK I HAVE EVER READ.<br />The writing is stilted, the story is dull, it doesn't make sense. The main character is a complete waste of space - I didn't like him at all, and was glad when bad things happened to him. There is no explanation for anything, and things happen for no reason at all; nothing is ever explained, or acknowledged. Things just happen, and are put across in this terrible attempt-funny style of writing that's just disjointed and lazy. Not to mention that the protag's condition and continual sympathy-seeking is shocking. OK, we get it, your mum's an exotic dancer, you live in a run-down house, you're some child prodigy scholarship kid, yet you talk like an idiot and don't have a grain of intelligence or sympathy. We don't need to hear, every second line, that you're poor and you've never had this much before - we don't need to hear constantly that you're hard done by, and then see you sabotage EVERYTHING your mother has worked for so you can feel like a tough guy. You are a lame, lame character. You have no admirable traits.<br />Phew.<br />Glad I got that off my chest. Do not read this book. It is a waste of time and brain cells. I'm surprised Kenyon even managed to get it published.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2024584752295162237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_186331100" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186331100" />
    <a title="Sita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5831199-sita"><img alt="Sita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506310723p2/5831199.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186331100?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">To YA/Action/Zombie/Vampire lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sita by: </span>
      Not really anyone...
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186331100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer891883995653445540">This was the first Sherrilyn Kennyon book I read, I actually read this before I read the Dark Hunter series and I loved it. I was in Dymocks one day with my Mum and two little sisters and she said I could pick a book. I contemplated and contemplated it was either this or something else. In the end I decided on Infinity. I am glad I did. I flew through it and despite it’s size I managed to read it in one afternoon and I read it again and again.<br/><br/><b>Plot in a sentence and a half: </b> Nick is 14 and is bul</span>
  <span id="freeText891883995653445540" style="display:none">This was the first Sherrilyn Kennyon book I read, I actually read this before I read the Dark Hunter series and I loved it. I was in Dymocks one day with my Mum and two little sisters and she said I could pick a book. I contemplated and contemplated it was either this or something else. In the end I decided on Infinity. I am glad I did. I flew through it and despite it’s size I managed to read it in one afternoon and I read it again and again.<br><br><b>Plot in a sentence and a half: </b> Nick is 14 and is bullied at school because he is poor and his Mum is kind of a stripper, but that’s not the story. So one day Nick is with his (so called) friends and they decide to mug an old couple, Nick steps in and stops it, they shoot him and were going to kill him if Kyrian (seen in Night Pleasures) hadn’t stepped in and saved him. He ends up being dragged into a world of Zombies, Vampires, tall Goth gods and general craziness.<br><br><b>What I thought of it: </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Boy this book was fast moving, this all happened over the space of a day and a bit. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380353434ra/706778.gif" width="499" height="254" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And it was over. I liked that. It was a great mix of action/zombies/cool people and bad guys. This is nothing like any of other Sherrilyn Kenyon’s other book; in the sense that romance is not the main theme. Sure it’s there, but it is a very, very small factor of the book (he’s 14 for goodness sake). This is a YA book; so don’t go in expecting a flat out romance.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353434i/706779.gif" width="240" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>The characters:</b> Too much to say. We get to see so many of the characters in the Dark Hunter worlds, younger versions of most of them. This is the perfect look into the Dark Hunter world and it’s characters. I would have read this book just for the characters (they are dead drop amazing). Here we see some of the best-developed characters (there are tonnes of them) I’ve seen in a while. Even the ones that were only in the book for a page or two leave a mark and are memorable. They all have different personalities. No one is one-dimensional.<br><br><b>The writing: </b> The writing is what got me hooked on Sherrilyn Kenyon. I loved this writing, the sarcasm, boy there was a lot of it, and the fist sentence says that. This has got to be one of the best first sentences I have ever read in a book. It had me laughing right from the first page.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380353434ra/706780.gif" width="500" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The book does not disappoint, there are so many great lines throughout the book and this is what I would consider a perfect YA novel (although some may disagree).<br><br><b>Overall:</b> Read it, it’s a great read. Almost all of my friends have read it, my copy is so used that it looks old, really old. And I only bought it about a year ago. I recommend this book to YA lovers. And despite the blurb this book is not a major book about Zombies. SO, don’t let your reservations on Zombies hold you back. I also recommend this book to Action/Zombie/Vampire lovers. This book is a great paranormal read. Can I say that enough?</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="891883995653445540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_123887719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123887719" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123887719?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781427209092" href="/book/show/6680655-infinity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123887719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2506163548052121257">I skimmed quite a bit through this one...and still feel I wasted a LOT of time. Yes...these are hours of my life I'll never get back.<br/><br/>The book dragged on trying to get started as we went to school with Nick and watched him persecuted more thoroughly than Bilbo at an Orc convention. We suffered through him having to live on powdered eggs...with maybe a little bacon, sometimes not even out of date (Nick's mom is poor but noble....not real understanding at times, but noble. Oh and also very importan</span>
  <span id="freeText2506163548052121257" style="display:none">I skimmed quite a bit through this one...and still feel I wasted a LOT of time. Yes...these are hours of my life I'll never get back.<br /><br />The book dragged on trying to get started as we went to school with Nick and watched him persecuted more thoroughly than Bilbo at an Orc convention. We suffered through him having to live on powdered eggs...with maybe a little bacon, sometimes not even out of date (Nick's mom is poor but noble....not real understanding at times, but noble. Oh and also very important, don't forget that, very important...take care of your mom). We struggled with Nick being misunderstood, abused, and just wronged. Then we finally got into the story. <br /><br />There were a few good humorous quips, references to pop-culture, movies, electronic games etc. and so on. But other than that I just got tired and burned out on zombies, time slips, demons and a story I just couldn't get into. (There are also warped mythological characters, shape shifters, "werebeasts"(werecritters?), "Daemons", and assorted other monsters including sort of putrid flying monkeys.) The book begins to tell a mildly interesting story about the last 2 chapters, but every time I got "mildly interested" the thing wandered off and managed to hit the annoyance button (specifics would contain spoilers...). Other than a few "story related" items like distorted folklore references, there were SOOOO MANY places where there were lines like "before he could answer another wave of zombies interrupted", or "I'll have to tell you that (important plot point) later, we're here". You get the picture?<br /><br />I didn't "hate" this book, it escapes a 1 star rating (barely...:) but it just didn't (for me) ever jell, it failed to hold together, it just didn't work. Sorry.<br /><br />I know however some will like it, taste is like that otherwise boiled okra, stinky cheese, Ator (The Fighting Eagle) movies, and Gilligan's Island would never have staid around as they have, so if you like it enjoy. As I said, it has it's moments. I even laughed at a few of the "quips", but the story didn't quite make it for me.<br /><br />By the way, did I say how annoying the book was at times???? </span>
  <a data-text-id="2506163548052121257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104190009" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104190009" />

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104190009?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie Garrison " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie Garrison " href="/user/show/2489609-laurie-garrison">Laurie Garrison </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104190009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1265002002297362320">This is totally a young adult book. If your looking for something like the dark hunters series, its not here, so you don’t get the romance and hardcore action. I would recommend this book to people who read YA books, but if YA is not your cup of tea like me, well you may want to read more than a couple of reviews before buying. There is action, and humor and teens that turns into zombies, yep, picture it, some of the football team as zombies coming after to kill Nick. <br/><br/>Nick starts out as a loser.</span>
  <span id="freeText1265002002297362320" style="display:none">This is totally a young adult book. If your looking for something like the dark hunters series, its not here, so you don’t get the romance and hardcore action. I would recommend this book to people who read YA books, but if YA is not your cup of tea like me, well you may want to read more than a couple of reviews before buying. There is action, and humor and teens that turns into zombies, yep, picture it, some of the football team as zombies coming after to kill Nick. <br /><br />Nick starts out as a loser. With his mom being a striper he ends up getting bullied all the time. One time some teen starts teasing Nick, he gets kicked out of school because of fighting that teen. That night he ends up in with some kids that tries to rob an old couple, he starts thinking this is not a good idea and ends up with the Teens beating the crap out of him, until Kyrian steps in. From there you’ll find there is someone after him and sending Zombies to kill him.<br /><br />You’ll see a few D-H in here, even Artemis makes an appearance. There is a few new characters you’ll meet one is Bubba. I really liked Bubba, he has two rules 1. "Shoot first then ask questions". 2. "Double tap just for good Measure". "Better safe than sorry". Bubba adds a lot of humor. He is the reason I had added a star to this rating.<br /><br />You’ll find a few things about Nick from the D-H’s told in more detail and some loose ends taken care of. But as a D-H reader I found Nick’s life not the same as portrayed as in the D-H books. Other than that I found the book dragged and was too boring. I want to stress if I was a YA reader that had never read the D-H series, my rating would be a lot higher. </span>

<div id="review_89526916" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89526916" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3050338-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474253068p2/3050338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89526916?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/3050338-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=young-adult-lit">young-adult-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer89526916&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89526916" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17857906565783321384">Infinity is the first book in Sherrilyn Kenyon's Chronicles of Nick series. This book starts with Nick at age fourteen when he is first introduced into the supernatural world: first by Kyrian saving him from being beaten to death by his "friends" and second after zombies attack at his school. His powers as the Malachai are slowly unleashed and Nick finally realizes that there is a world out there that he never knew about.<br/><br/>I loved finally starting to learn more about Nick. I mean, we know some thi</span>
  <span id="freeText17857906565783321384" style="display:none">Infinity is the first book in Sherrilyn Kenyon's Chronicles of Nick series. This book starts with Nick at age fourteen when he is first introduced into the supernatural world: first by Kyrian saving him from being beaten to death by his "friends" and second after zombies attack at his school. His powers as the Malachai are slowly unleashed and Nick finally realizes that there is a world out there that he never knew about.<br /><br />I loved finally starting to learn more about Nick. I mean, we know some things about him from the Dark-Hunter series, but we never <i>really</i> knew anything about him. Nick is much more complicated than anyone could ever imagine, even at such a young age. I found him highly amusing and entertaining throughout the novel, and he was extremely witty and intelligent. I liked that, even though he was considered less important than the rich people, he had morals, values, and was still kind to others.<br /><br />I found it interesting that Cherise grated on my nerves quite a bit throughout the novel. I understand that she is a mother and they are often overprotective, but it bothered me quite a bit; maybe more so than it bothered Nick. I mean, she never let the poor boy get a word in edgewise when he was trying to explain something to her! Anyway, I still like Cherise (and still feel horrible about what later happens to her).<br /><br />Kyrian...Ohhhh, Kyrian. It was so nice to see him when he came into this novel. I loved the way he helped Nick out and how unconcerned he was by the fact that his housekeeper knows how to wield a knife and is not afraid to use it. Can't wait to catch more of him in the upcoming CON books.<br /><br />Along with Kyrian, we also get a few glimpses of Acheron. It's always a treat to see Ash, and it was interesting to read his thoughts on how important Nick was going to come to be in his life. His interaction with Nick in the car on the ride to Nick's house was entertaining as hell because they were both being highly sarcastic. As always, my love, it was great to see you, Ash!<br /><br />I did not like the fact that Nick met Simi. He's not supposed to meet her for the first time until he's twenty-four in Seize the Night.<br /><br />I cannot tell you how much I loved seeing Tabitha in this book. She is my favorite female from the DH series and so I was absolutely ecstatic to see her fighting vampires (who are actually DAIMONS!) and zombies in this book.<br /><br />Eric was awesome. Enough said.<br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed seeing a bit of Adarian in this book. We know even less about him than we do Nick. It was cool to see a little bit of him in prison and get a feel for him. I mean, aside from knowing he is a psychotic murderer, we don't know that much about the man so I look forward to seeing more of him in future Chronicles of Nick books.<br /><br />Ugh. Stone. I wanted to reach into the book and punch him. Obviously I recognized him from Bad Moon Rising so I knew who he was but this book just made him more of a bastard in my opinion. Therefore, I found great joy when he was whimpering like a baby when the zombies had him.<br /><br />Ambrose...Grown-up Nick...I'm not exactly sure how I feel about having the grown-up Nick there with younger Nick. It was very, very weird for me.<br /><br />I am not exactly sure how I feel about Caleb. Is he working for Adarian? Is he working for Ambrose? Is he really there to protect Nick? Is he there for something more sinister? How does all this affect him?<br /><br />For the two seconds that Artemis was in the book, I wanted to kill her. Just ew. Gag me. Blech. Ugh. Grr.<br /><br />Like with Caleb, I am not sure about Nekoda. Is she there to help Nick? Will she kill Nick? Is she good? Is she evil? What side is she <i>really</i> on? Also, I absolutely did not like her kissing on my Nicky (Yes, he's mine. Deal with it.).<br /><br />I loved Bubba and Mark.<br /><br />Overall, it was a fantastic book and I highly recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17857906565783321384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_306452227" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306452227" />
    <a title="Hitandmiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5020457-hitandmiss"><img alt="Hitandmiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307918549p2/5020457.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306452227?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hitandmiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hitandmiss" href="/user/show/5020457-hitandmiss">Hitandmiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5020457-hitandmiss?shelf=got-board">got-board</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306452227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17262376327322247523">“Couldn’t finish the book” Review – I couldn’t stop rolling my eyes, How contrived a narrative can you force onto people to try to make them sympathise and like a character? I found Nick so badly written and all the people who he talks too so stereotyped into a box I couldn’t even get into the real plot.<br/><br/>Nick;<br/>He’s poor,<br/>Smart but nerdy,<br/>Doesn’t have any friends,<br/>He’s really really poor,<br/>He’s from a broken dysfunctional home, so he doesn’t have a dad or any connection to his grandparents,<br/>He’s bullied,</span>
  <span id="freeText17262376327322247523" style="display:none">“Couldn’t finish the book” Review – I couldn’t stop rolling my eyes, How contrived a narrative can you force onto people to try to make them sympathise and like a character? I found Nick so badly written and all the people who he talks too so stereotyped into a box I couldn’t even get into the real plot.<br /><br />Nick;<br />He’s poor,<br />Smart but nerdy,<br />Doesn’t have any friends,<br />He’s really really poor,<br />He’s from a broken dysfunctional home, so he doesn’t have a dad or any connection to his grandparents,<br />He’s bullied, because he’s dirt poor,<br />His mom and his surrogate family all work at a strip/Pole dancing club.<br />He has terrible clothes,<br />He’s shot helping old people,<br />He’s Super poor.<br />His teachers hate him because he’s riff raff from a poor dirt poor home with a bad mother!<br /><br />Oh and he’s poor!<br /><br />The author really needs to learn the basic story telling method of Showing us rather than telling us, getting told 50 times that Nick is poor and how everyone hates him for it is soooo childish and lame its reality breaking, his teachers would sympathise with him (They love honor students, they want to teach not lambast the poor!) No one is this clownishly evil, rich people might look down on the poor, but they wouldn’t be so stereotypical about it. I was waiting for the rich kids to pay there butlers to beat him up, or to stone him with gold bars.<br /><br />I got up to Bubba (Double degree holding Psychopath?) and the goth vampire killer (super hot, like every other girl hes ran into so far?) before I had to quit, I realise I might be slightly too old for this book, but I couldn’t imagine a young adult reading this and sympathising with Nick.<br /><br />I really am supprised that this got past an editor, It shows soo little finesse it was little better then some fan fiction. The only way to make this worse was if Nick was forced to live under some stairs (:P)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17262376327322247523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697459010?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer697459010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5552990481319277176">Infinity is the first book of Sherrilyn Kenyon that I've read and probably will be the last because heck, there's a lot of books in this series (and it's still on-going) and a lot more books in the same universe. I'm #shookt. I would probably read another book of her if it's not included in this so-called Dark Hunter universe. Or whatsoever.<br/><br/>Anyway, I still enjoyed reading this book. There is no denying that fact. Infinity has a decent story line, a set of interesting characters and every page fu</span>
  <span id="freeText5552990481319277176" style="display:none">Infinity is the first book of Sherrilyn Kenyon that I've read and probably will be the last because heck, there's a lot of books in this series (and it's still on-going) and a lot more books in the same universe. I'm #shookt. I would probably read another book of her if it's not included in this so-called Dark Hunter universe. Or whatsoever.<br /><br />Anyway, I still enjoyed reading this book. There is no denying that fact. Infinity has a decent story line, a set of interesting characters and every page full of heavy sarcasm. I love it!<br /><br />Basically, it is about clueless Nick and how he discovers his demonic abilities. From being clueless to being a hero, a lot of things has happened in-between. And from zombies, vampires, shapeshifters, different demons and demon-hunters to Greek goddess, Infinity has it all. <br /><br />It's all good but it also becomes confusing especially to a reader who hasn't read any books from the Dark Hunter universe. Sure, readers of this series will not find it confusing but I am not them. I can say it does lack of world building for a first-timer like me in this universe.<br /><br />Infinity still compels and intrigues me, to be honest. I want to know more about Nick and his colleagues. But, seeing the books in this series is somehow discouraging. Maybe when I run out of books to be read (which is not gonna happen), I will pursue reading the series. But for now, I don't think so.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5552990481319277176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1376705686764302072">I enjoyed this first installment of CON. Sherrilyn Kenyon has convinced me with her talent. She was able to keep me wrapped up in the world she created for Nick. Be it adult romance or young adult fantasy, she's built a solid foundation with intriguing creatures. <br/><br/>Nick is a 14 years old and dirt poor. His Mom is a stripper and they eat substituted food like powdered eggs. I am not sure if Nick feels bad about his home situation because his his attitude is so acidic at times. I'll sting you, befor</span>
  <span id="freeText1376705686764302072" style="display:none">I enjoyed this first installment of CON. Sherrilyn Kenyon has convinced me with her talent. She was able to keep me wrapped up in the world she created for Nick. Be it adult romance or young adult fantasy, she's built a solid foundation with intriguing creatures. <br /><br />Nick is a 14 years old and dirt poor. His Mom is a stripper and they eat substituted food like powdered eggs. I am not sure if Nick feels bad about his home situation because his his attitude is so acidic at times. I'll sting you, before you burn me. <br /><br />When the inevitable paranormal antics ensue, Nick's seems almost blase'. To be fair Sherrilyn Kenyon writes the scenes with an air of humor. Revealing the enemy as something of interest instead of crap your pants horror. Nick's reaction is very 21st century teen. His crush on Nekoda will be something to look out for. <br /><br />The plot of Infinity varies from Nick being introduced to Kyrian, to him fighting supernatural creatures and having NO idea there are others right beside him fighting along with him. Ash makes an appearance for all you DH fans =D <br /><br />In all it is worth investing in this series if your a fan of Sherrilyn Kenyon/Dark Hunters. It is fun seeing the Dark Hunters from Nick's POV, because its all new to him. Also non-Dark Hunter fans you don't have to read the Dark Hunters series to enjoy CON but I highly recommend you get intimate with Kyrian and Ash at the very least, and any other main characters introduced in the CON series. WARNING: The Dark Hunters series in meant for adults and has adult content.<br /><br />*********************************PLOT/SPOILER ALERT*******************<br />Nick himself is a powerful being that even Ash is concerned about. The reason there will be 10 books in this series, I'm guessing, is because Nick has 10 lessons to learn to hone his skills. 'Uncle Ambrose' warns him about holding a grudge. Remember what happens between Ash and Nick? I was getting chills when Ambrose was trying hard to break that hold over Nick's heart to want revenge for what happened to Nick at 14. </span>

<div id="review_115076124" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115076124" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2871271-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1258152693p2/2871271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115076124?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/2871271-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115076124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4984386361504382343">Disappointing addition to young adult paranormal genre<br/><br/>Having never read any of the Dark-Hunter books, I came into Kenyon's INFINITY: CHRONICLES OF NICK without expectations. Unfortunately, Kenyon's foray into the young adult genre left me extremely disappointed. As the book opens, we meet Nick, a scrappy but sullen fourteen-year-old boy who lives with his mother in the slums of New Orleans. After being shot during an attempted mugging one night, Nick is saved by a mysterious man who takes him un</span>
  <span id="freeText4984386361504382343" style="display:none">Disappointing addition to young adult paranormal genre<br /><br />Having never read any of the Dark-Hunter books, I came into Kenyon's INFINITY: CHRONICLES OF NICK without expectations. Unfortunately, Kenyon's foray into the young adult genre left me extremely disappointed. As the book opens, we meet Nick, a scrappy but sullen fourteen-year-old boy who lives with his mother in the slums of New Orleans. After being shot during an attempted mugging one night, Nick is saved by a mysterious man who takes him under his wing. As Nick's time with his new mentor continues, he slowly learns about an otherworld he didn't know existed and his potential role in it. Soon, zombies start terrorizing the city, and Nick finds himself at the center of a ragtag group who must try to stop them. <br /><br />First and foremost, this book should be marketed for middle-grade readers, not young adults. The writing was elementary and simplistic, which is not how a young adult novel should read, even if the characters are young. The writing felt lazy with weak descriptions and an overreliance on supposed "teen speak" like Nick saying "Gah!" all the time. Little to no character development occurred among the main characters, and all of the secondary characters were flat. The plot itself felt silly and contrived, since it was clear there was never any real threat. As a non-Dark-Hunter reader, the mythology was confusing and remained unclear at the end of the book. This muddled mythology contributed to the poor world building, which was so minimal that I was never able to suspend belief and immerse myself in the created world. Completely illogical things happened, even for an urban fantasy, like immortals disclosing secret information to Nick within minutes of meeting him or kissing scenes while zombies were literally trying to eat the characters. <br /><br />Among the few positives, INFINITY may appeal to young male audiences with its focus on action, instead of romance. Younger readers may enjoy the dialogue and find it humorous, and the story did end with a finished conclusion (no cliffhanger), which I always appreciate. For existing fans of Kenyon's adult Dark-Hunter series, this novel may also provide backstory for characters they've followed in her other books. <br /><br />Overall, Kenyon's attempt to jump into the young adult market with INFINITY disappointed me with its inability to create a world I would want to visit again. As an adult reader, it also failed to entice me to pick up her adult series. If you're a fan of adult urban fantasy and would like to see a good addition to the young adult world by one of your favorite authors, I highly recommend Kelley Armstrong's Darkest Powers series (THE SUMMONING, Book 1) instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4984386361504382343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer126953227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14133918672477681281">I didn’t start this with positive thoughts. My reasons were:<br/>• I didn’t depart the Dark Hunter series with the best feelings;<br/>• Never really liked Nick;<br/>• Wasn’t sure of Sherrilyn Kenyon’s ability to write a good YA novel.<br/><br/>Did I make a good choice with <i>Infinity</i>? Will the <i>Chronicles of Nick</i> rock your world? Well no and no. Sorry Nicky boy, you’re just not cool enough. Yet.<br/><br/>The book lacks a proper story. All I got was Nick being bullied, Nick lacking food and Nick being chased by stupid jock zombies (c</span>
  <span id="freeText14133918672477681281" style="display:none">I didn’t start this with positive thoughts. My reasons were:<br>• I didn’t depart the Dark Hunter series with the best feelings;<br>• Never really liked Nick;<br>• Wasn’t sure of Sherrilyn Kenyon’s ability to write a good YA novel.<br><br>Did I make a good choice with <i>Infinity</i>? Will the <i>Chronicles of Nick</i> rock your world? Well no and no. Sorry Nicky boy, you’re just not cool enough. Yet.<br><br>The book lacks a proper story. All I got was Nick being bullied, Nick lacking food and Nick being chased by stupid jock zombies (cheesy much?). As much as I love these filthy creatures the book got me depressed. <br><br><i>Infinity</i> didn’t even elaborate the Dark Hunter-related things I wanted to find out. I wouldn’t mind this if the events in the book were funny/interesting/romantic/sentimental/whatever. The story just goes around in circles, some supernatural elements get thrown around mindlessly, and the characters don’t even evolve. Nothing seems to get me attracted towards reading more. I have absolutely no feelings for any of the relevant characters (put the old ones like Ash, Tabitha, Simi, Kyrian aside). If I think about it, there’s absolutely nothing that I like about this book. No, wait! I actually liked one thing. I’ll make it cryptic to avoid spoilers: “the present meeting the future” (lol I guess some mysterious music would work wonderfully with this). That was a nice touch and the only thing that saved the book from getting one star.<br><br>Since I’m curious to see what Nicky will manage to do, I’m going to give the next book a try. <br><br>See you next time on <b>How Jock Zombies Will Eat Your Brain</b>!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340603i/696980._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14133918672477681281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/516624988" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/516624988?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula" href="/user/show/6721230-paula">Paula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer516624988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5083193305635906015">It started off as a relatively inocuous fun YA read. The characters are clever and silly and it was entertaining.. at first. <br/>Then it jumps the shark as the author begins introducing so many different creatures people and empty hinted at story lines that never come to fruition. She makes a HUGE sloppy mess of it. A fun read devolves into a convoluted non-nonsensical almost indecipherable mess.<br/><br/>Its like the horror section at the video store threw up and the author expects me to clean it. ADHD much?</span>
  <span id="freeText5083193305635906015" style="display:none">It started off as a relatively inocuous fun YA read. The characters are clever and silly and it was entertaining.. at first. <br />Then it jumps the shark as the author begins introducing so many different creatures people and empty hinted at story lines that never come to fruition. She makes a HUGE sloppy mess of it. A fun read devolves into a convoluted non-nonsensical almost indecipherable mess.<br /><br />Its like the horror section at the video store threw up and the author expects me to clean it. ADHD much? Zombies- the dead kind, which come about spontaneously (I think) and the living kind (which were created accidentally on purpose by kid who made a video game he could play to inflict mind control on others that goes haywire) another kid with unspecified supernatural connections, his uncle, who's really him in a previous incarnation, except they're both still alive, his evil father who has another supernatural genus/species I dont recall, vampires, warewolves, daemons, demons (I read the book and Im still not sure what the difference is), gods, simis (also got me) and a half a dozen unfleshed out (no pun intended) other types of supernatural beings.. I kept thinking "what? who?" Its a complicated-for-no-reason hot mess. I want to grab her and shake her till she makes a decision! <br /><br />Maybe she straightens it all out by the third book, but this is the written version of a hoarders episode and I cant imagine a big enough pay off to make me wade through this much junk to put the author's house in order.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5083193305635906015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2062207167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4989475852917885085">3* dnf: 50% (read online) HOMEBOY NEEDS JESUS AND THIS IS COMING FROM AN ATHEIST SO WHAT IN THE GOD DAMN<br/><br/>This has to be one of the STUPIDEST books I've ever read, BUT it's also pretty entertaining. Unfortunately I hate books where the mortal world mixes with the other world/powers. So all the demon characters were interesting, but the parts of the book with Nick's interactions with mortals were torture to read. A lot of this book felt like set up for future books instead of a cohesive plot line f</span>
  <span id="freeText4989475852917885085" style="display:none">3* dnf: 50% (read online) HOMEBOY NEEDS JESUS AND THIS IS COMING FROM AN ATHEIST SO WHAT IN THE GOD DAMN<br /><br />This has to be one of the STUPIDEST books I've ever read, BUT it's also pretty entertaining. Unfortunately I hate books where the mortal world mixes with the other world/powers. So all the demon characters were interesting, but the parts of the book with Nick's interactions with mortals were torture to read. A lot of this book felt like set up for future books instead of a cohesive plot line for this one book. The unanswered mysterious questions of the book were interesting, but there were way too many unanswered questions to the point where this singular book had no purpose besides intrigue for future books. I tried to roll with the stupidity and see it in a fun light, but it was just too much for me.<br /><br />The main reason I can't stand this book is the main character Nick. People in the book say he charming, but he's probably one of my least favorite main characters of all time. He always says things like "don't help me" and "I'm a man". He really REALLY wants to be macho and have a super hot girlfriend. He's pretty gross and unrealistic for a 14 year old. Also I couldn't stand his mom either. She was super annoying. The way Nick thinks about women is over exaggerated, horny, and not something I'd like to read about.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4989475852917885085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1495636148?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia Generali" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia Generali" href="/user/show/13207034-sofia-generali">Sofia Generali</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer13153996268030286794"><b>NOPE, NOPE, NOPE. NEVER AGAIN. This was..... so bad... I just.... I can't</b><br/><br/>I've only ever given a book 1 star ONCE before now. That alone should tell you how much I disliked this book!!<br/><br/><b>1/5 stars</b><br/>(just a warning, there may be slight spoilers in this. This review mainly a rant though so there shouldn't be many spoilers, if any)<br/><br/>Hmmmm how exactly do I say this?<br/>Oh, I know! <b>This book was a <i>mess</i></b><br/><br/>SERIOUSLY. The writing style was, frankly, terrible. This is probably the worst writing I've ever experienced in</span>
  <span id="freeText13153996268030286794" style="display:none"><b>NOPE, NOPE, NOPE. NEVER AGAIN. This was..... so bad... I just.... I can't</b><br /><br />I've only ever given a book 1 star ONCE before now. That alone should tell you how much I disliked this book!!<br /><br /><b>1/5 stars</b><br />(just a warning, there may be slight spoilers in this. This review mainly a rant though so there shouldn't be many spoilers, if any)<br /><br />Hmmmm how exactly do I say this?<br />Oh, I know! <b>This book was a <i>mess</i></b><br /><br />SERIOUSLY. The writing style was, frankly, terrible. This is probably the worst writing I've ever experienced in a book tbh. It was so childish and just so entirely unbelievable.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The "storyline"</u>
</b><br />Quotation marks bc what even was this??<br /><b>FIRST</b> we get a protagonist hated by E V E R Y O N E, even his principal (which, tbh, I found wayyyyyy too unrealistic for my liking). THEN we get a whole host of characters that are just not developed enough and very unrealistic. <br /><br /><b>SOMEHOW</b> a character allllllwayyyyys says something philosophical and deep and basically plot-hinty at every possible chance and we're expected to take it seriously. And I typically LOVE philosophical thoughts, but in this context, everything said was just so impossible. Seriously, nobody SAYS the things characters say in this book.<br /><br /><b>THEN ALL OF A SUDDEN, OUT OF THE FRICKIN BLUE, CANNIBALISM??? LIKE???? WTF???</b> Seriously, that was expected to fit into the storyline with very few qualms from anyone. And there was basically no forewarning whatsoever O-o<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br />I? was? not? a? fan? of? this?<br /><br />I will admit, sometimes the snark was entertaining, and the idea behind the book had the potential to be interesting, but this novel was just gone about all wrong. There was TOO MUCH snark, believe it or not. It actually got tiresome! <br /><br /><b>THE PORTRAYAL OF FEMALE CHARACTERS WAS A SOLID NOPE FOR ME.</b> SERIOUSLY, every character was either "smokin' hot" (ew I hate that phrase) or really quirky, flat-out strange, and somewhat unintelligent. Also, Nick CONTINUOUSLY acted as though every girl needed his protection and it pissed me the fuck off. Ooooooo boy I disliked this. I also felt no inclination towards Nick's mother, who never listened to him and yelled at him for the majority of the time she saw him, never really recognizing wtf was going on in his life.<br /><br /><b>Ughhhhh</b><br /><br />It's been a long time since a book pissed me off so much. I just can't deal with it. I acknowledge that this book was a positive experience for other people, and maybe they saw things that I didn't. Regardless, I stand firm with my 1 star rating and with everything I've said thus far.<br /><br />I just, I can't. I really can't. Too many aspects of this book (unrealistic characters, weak writing, low-key sexist portrayal of female characters, unrealistic dialogue, etc, etc) felt lacking to me, and all I can say is I'm majorly disappointed. I was looking forward to an action-packed narrative to lose myself in, but <b>this was not it.</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8795848499474215240">This book is terrible! I might have been more interested if the writing wouldn't have been as bad. This book is written in the 3rd person, but it seemed as if she was confused as to who the main character was. All of the characters are written together and "thinking" and "saying" things at the same time and you have no idea who is thinking or saying what. After getting past that, the possible main character, Nick, is not even close to relatable. It's as if she was trying to make him a comedian b</span>
  <span id="freeText8795848499474215240" style="display:none">This book is terrible! I might have been more interested if the writing wouldn't have been as bad. This book is written in the 3rd person, but it seemed as if she was confused as to who the main character was. All of the characters are written together and "thinking" and "saying" things at the same time and you have no idea who is thinking or saying what. After getting past that, the possible main character, Nick, is not even close to relatable. It's as if she was trying to make him a comedian but all of the jokes fall flat. I'm not exaggerating; literally EVERY joke, quip, or attempt at whittery fails miserably. This might be the most annoying main character ever! Then, if you're able to get past all of that, there's the plot/plots? At first you think this story is about Nick discovering who he is, but then it becomes a story fully centered on the possible zombie apocalypse, but then, it's about 30 other things. Nothing feels connected! Needless to say, Chronicles of Nick will be stopping and ending with book 1 for me. Good luck to anyone who wants to read this series. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1569049711?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chance Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chance Lee" href="/user/show/2355889-chance-lee">Chance Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312603045" href="/book/show/9676673-infinity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2355889-chance-lee?shelf=ya-no">ya-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2355889-chance-lee?shelf=shmoop">shmoop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1569049711" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17019794543763017453">Reading this book is like looking into a shoebox filled with colorless shrinky dinks. (<a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.michaels.com/shrinky-dinks/M10183880.html'>http://www.michaels.com/shrinky-dinks...</a>)<br/>There are many characters, and all of them are one-dimensional. Despite being set in New Orleans, Kenyon grossly misuses her setting, never once describing it. In her book, the city is dull, featureless, and empty. <br/>In "Infinity," Nick Gautier is your stereotypical chosen one. He has powers, maybe? And powerful beings watch over him, or something? And zombie type creatur</span>
  <span id="freeText17019794543763017453" style="display:none">Reading this book is like looking into a shoebox filled with colorless shrinky dinks. (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.michaels.com/shrinky-dinks/M10183880.html">http://www.michaels.com/shrinky-dinks...</a>)<br />There are many characters, and all of them are one-dimensional. Despite being set in New Orleans, Kenyon grossly misuses her setting, never once describing it. In her book, the city is dull, featureless, and empty. <br />In "Infinity," Nick Gautier is your stereotypical chosen one. He has powers, maybe? And powerful beings watch over him, or something? And zombie type creatures attack? And they defeat them. <br />Nothing in this book is original. Ancient powers threaten the world. One boy is the chosen one to defeat them all. The humor relies on tired old Chuck Norris jokes. <br />The funniest thing about this book is that Sherrilyn Kenyon is suing Cassandra Clare for plagiarism. Does Kenyon understand that everything in her book is an archetype, trope, or stereotype? Even accusing Cassandra Clare of plagiarism is so 2001. <br />I've read a lot of brain-dead young-adult books, but this might be one of the absolute dumbest. The writing is terrible, there isn't enough plot to sustain its length, and what little plot there is feels slapdash and inconsistent. There is no main villain. There is no clear plot arc. <br />Last year, I thought the Violets of Smarch was the dumbest book I'd ever read. This one undercuts that one by miles, so I'm glad I gave Smarch two stars. The floor gets even lower. <br />Infinity can barely be considered a book. It is much less than the sum of its parts. The only thing holding it together is a physical cover. I expect its spine to disintegrate, its pages to blow away, and the words on them to peel off like loose threads, dissolving into little puffs of ink in the air. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17019794543763017453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2385549286" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385549286" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58578943-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471012163p2/58578943.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2385549286?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/58578943-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58578943-jennifer?shelf=imagine-that">imagine-that</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58578943-jennifer?shelf=i-can-t-adult-today">i-can-t-adult-today</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58578943-jennifer?shelf=challenge">challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385549286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4220292335065371052">Nick already has plenty of struggles in his life - he's poor, constantly has to defend his exotic dancer of a mother, and he is smart enough to want to stay out of trouble despite society's pressures to keep him in the gutter. It seems that he is destined to feel more struggles as supernatural begin to influence him as well when he is rescued from a beating by a Dark Hunter and exposed to the supernatural world. <br/><br/>This story is pretty action-packed. I was surprised when there was a zombie outbreak</span>
  <span id="freeText4220292335065371052" style="display:none">Nick already has plenty of struggles in his life - he's poor, constantly has to defend his exotic dancer of a mother, and he is smart enough to want to stay out of trouble despite society's pressures to keep him in the gutter. It seems that he is destined to feel more struggles as supernatural begin to influence him as well when he is rescued from a beating by a Dark Hunter and exposed to the supernatural world. <br /><br />This story is pretty action-packed. I was surprised when there was a zombie outbreak at Nick's school - just didn't' see that one coming and it was very entertaining. I thought the use of the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ video game <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> as a catalyst for the zombie infection was pretty clever. Definitely something that would appeal to younger readers, although there was some bad language so maybe not too young. Nakoda's character and her mysterious role in Nick's fate are intriguing. I'd like to keep going with the series just to find out more about her. I'd like to give it a higher rating, but I'm still a little confused about who is evil and who isn't and how the battle lines are being drawn, but that's ok. I still liked the story and have high hopes that it will become more clear in the next book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4220292335065371052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156226210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8164731139417773392">Oh that was entertaining!!! This is also the first book I ready from Mrs Kenyon, yeah I know - shame on me. But I think I'm glad I started with her YA series before digging into the mature stuff. ;) <br/><br/>The cover always crabbed me but somehow I never picked it up, I guess I was afraid when I read Nick is supposed to be 14 and this sounds more MG than YA to me - but..duhh! I'm glad I did now, I truly enjoyed myself and I will most definitely go and buy the next one right away. <br/><br/>This is the very rich s</span>
  <span id="freeText8164731139417773392" style="display:none">Oh that was entertaining!!! This is also the first book I ready from Mrs Kenyon, yeah I know - shame on me. But I think I'm glad I started with her YA series before digging into the mature stuff. ;) <br /><br />The cover always crabbed me but somehow I never picked it up, I guess I was afraid when I read Nick is supposed to be 14 and this sounds more MG than YA to me - but..duhh! I'm glad I did now, I truly enjoyed myself and I will most definitely go and buy the next one right away. <br /><br />This is the very rich story about Nick and his struggle against evil and his true self, although he has no clue yet what that means. He's a poor kid that lives with his mum, his dad is an evil psychopath that is in jail. He has a scholarship to go to a school full of rick kids. And yeah, they are not very nice to him. <br /><br />Nik's voice is awesome and super funny. His sarcasm and snarkiness totally got me and I found myself smiling at this smart ass :) He definitely doesn't take crap from anyone and is too smart for his own good. But. the way he deeply cares about his mom is wonderful! <br /><br />Nik finds himself suddenly in a world full of paranormal creatures and it is happening all way too fast for him to grab. Also, apparently he is something special too although he doesn't want to believe it. Many creatures want to get a hold of him and according to a some sources if he turns evil he will doom the world. So, the good people want to do anything to prevent this. Still, Nik has no clue about all of this! <br /><br />This is one of those stories that move forward merciless and are thick with new developments fast. I love such rich stories, they keep you on edge all the time. Also, she created a world full of Demons, Shifters, Vampires and ancient gods. I love when an author is able to create a world that big. <br /><br />But what I loved most is Nik! I loved his sense of humor, his braveness and his sarcasm! Now, excuse me, I go and read the next one!! <br /></span>

<div id="review_186324602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186324602" />
    <a title="Katie O&#39;Sullivan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11702136-katie-o-sullivan"><img alt="Katie O&#39;Sullivan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442510845p2/11702136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186324602?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie O&#39;Sullivan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie O&#39;Sullivan" href="/user/show/11702136-katie-o-sullivan">Katie O&#39;Sullivan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186324602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9534473612541996078">There was much to like about this book's premise and some of the characters, but I was left uncomfortable in reading it by the many inconsistencies of both language and characters. For example... The main characters mother is a stripper who dropped out of school to have a baby, yet she always speaks very properly. The main character himself speaks properly (almost adult-like in his syntax in thought and word) for the first 80 pages and then seems to remember he's one step up from a street kid an</span>
  <span id="freeText9534473612541996078" style="display:none">There was much to like about this book's premise and some of the characters, but I was left uncomfortable in reading it by the many inconsistencies of both language and characters. For example... The main characters mother is a stripper who dropped out of school to have a baby, yet she always speaks very properly. The main character himself speaks properly (almost adult-like in his syntax in thought and word) for the first 80 pages and then seems to remember he's one step up from a street kid and starts throwing "ain't" into every other sentence for the next big chunk of the story. He claims he's never had a t.v. or gaming console (too poor), but makes myriad pop references to both (which bothered my son more than it did me, I must admit) You're not ever quite sure who is a good guy and who is a bad guy, which isn't always a bad thing and can in fact make for excellent reading... but in this case it really bothered me because you want to care about this kid and want him to make good choices, but those choices are so completely and utterly murky you're left not knowing what to hope for. I did read the book all the way to the end, but was left wishing I'd spent the time reading something better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9534473612541996078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2276066066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15969128574763614384">Infinity ⭐️<br/>I read this when it first came out along with the rest of the series and I still really like it. <br/>Nick is poor, not popular and pretty much basic by anyone’s standpoint until Kyrain a mysterious man finds him (beaten almost to death and brings him to the hospital, saving him) and offers him a job. Nick will soon discover all the magic and amazement of this world he once knew. <br/>Its a quick read and the writing flows wonderfully. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_105601981" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105601981" />
    <a title="Zeek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2478293-zeek"><img alt="Zeek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339154824p2/2478293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105601981?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zeek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zeek" href="/user/show/2478293-zeek">Zeek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=pnr-kitchen-sink">pnr-kitchen-sink</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=vamps">vamps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=angels-gods-demons">angels-gods-demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105601981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5012543241026266004">Surprisingly, I liked Infinity. I think I’m gonna have to re-think my YA phobia- and there is no doubt this is a YA. <br/><br/>Nick Gautier, introduced in Kenyon’s popular Dark Hunter series, is- or was- and now is- a squire (aka errand boy) for Dark Hunter Kryian Thrace. (FYI: Dark Hunters, among other things, are vampiric-type demon hunters whom only come out at night. Sorta. But not really.) <br/><br/>In Infinity, we get the beginning of the story- when Kyrian (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84150.Night_Pleasures__Dark_Hunter___2_' title='Night Pleasures (Dark-Hunter, #2) by Sherrilyn Kenyon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Night Pleasures</a>) saves Nick from a pack of hoodlums</span>
  <span id="freeText5012543241026266004" style="display:none">Surprisingly, I liked Infinity. I think I’m gonna have to re-think my YA phobia- and there is no doubt this is a YA. <br /><br />Nick Gautier, introduced in Kenyon’s popular Dark Hunter series, is- or was- and now is- a squire (aka errand boy) for Dark Hunter Kryian Thrace. (FYI: Dark Hunters, among other things, are vampiric-type demon hunters whom only come out at night. Sorta. But not really.) <br /><br />In Infinity, we get the beginning of the story- when Kyrian (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/84150.Night_Pleasures__Dark_Hunter___2_" title="Night Pleasures (Dark-Hunter, #2) by Sherrilyn Kenyon" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Pleasures</a>) saves Nick from a pack of hoodlums and takes the 14 yr old under his wing. Meanwhile a Zombie breakout at Nick’s highschool has occurred and it almost looks like Nick’s the reason for it- well him and the rich kid gamer who created the whole mess. It’ll take a good looking redneck named Bubba and his pack of followers to bring them down- and alotta interference from a mysterious creature named Ambrose who seems to know everything about him.<br /><br />Meanwhile we get a peek at Nick as he enters the world of Dark Hunters- and his true nature, which is still pretty much a mystery, to us AND him…<br /><br />Seriously, I found Infinity to be more coherent then some of her more recent “adult” novels, certainly more engaging- even though the whole Zombie thing is a side issue from what’s really going on-mainly, what the frack is a Malachi and will Ambrose <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ie: Future Nick <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> accomplish his goal of unlocking young Nick’s untapped powers- waaaay earlier then they’re supposed to be. <br /><br />After reading so many of Kenyon’s books I pretty much get that she had a crappy childhood, (Well hello SK Daddy issues, once again) and her writing is her way of justifying putting a noble spin on hating the ones who did her bad, (I always have to brush away the victim whininess and fanicifully preachy clichés she infuses into some of her characters), but goddangit, I always end up enjoying the ride. <br /><br />3.5 out of 5 from me </span>
  <a data-text-id="5012543241026266004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
